<div id="review_132486002" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/132486002" />
    <a title="Justin Kemppainen" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3293675-justin-kemppainen"><img alt="Justin Kemppainen" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/m_50x66-82093808bca726cb3249a493fbd3bd0f.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/132486002?book_show_action=true">Nov 26, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Justin Kemppainen" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Justin Kemppainen" href="/user/show/3293675-justin-kemppainen">Justin Kemppainen</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer132486002" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16039505751695652770">I had a hard time overall with the Faded Sun. The mri are a fascinating species, but their existence and survivability in the face of a refusal to adapt and change confuses me. I know it's a huge theme of the book, and it remains compelling all the way through, but on occasion I had a hard time suspending the disbelief. It would seem to me, correctly or otherwise, that such a rigid and unyielding code of life would not lend itself to long-term survival. Indeed it *nearly* didn't, but I wouldn't </span>
  <span id="freeText16039505751695652770" style="display:none">I had a hard time overall with the Faded Sun. The mri are a fascinating species, but their existence and survivability in the face of a refusal to adapt and change confuses me. I know it's a huge theme of the book, and it remains compelling all the way through, but on occasion I had a hard time suspending the disbelief. It would seem to me, correctly or otherwise, that such a rigid and unyielding code of life would not lend itself to long-term survival. Indeed it *nearly* didn't, but I wouldn't expect a society like that to get anywhere at all.<br /><br />In either case, the books were still quite good. Cherryh has a bit of a drier nature to her writing, but the story was definitely compelling enough to see all the way through.</span>
  <a data-text-id="16039505751695652770" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_1133474120" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1133474120" />
    <a title="Tom" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8589614-tom"><img alt="Tom" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1453910510p2/8589614.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1133474120?book_show_action=true">Dec 16, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Tom" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Tom" href="/user/show/8589614-tom">Tom</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1133474120" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11375573644317611168">THE FADED SUN is a wonderful story. Strangely, this was my first introduction to Cherryh. I was impressed so much that I am now on a quest to own her entire body of work. The Faded Sun is so rich in plot, location, and prose that those traits alone would make it worth reading. The story is exciting and full of wonder. However, the true beauty of this book is in the development of character. I am sure we have all read works in which we enjoyed the story but could have cared less about the charact</span>
  <span id="freeText11375573644317611168" style="display:none">THE FADED SUN is a wonderful story. Strangely, this was my first introduction to Cherryh. I was impressed so much that I am now on a quest to own her entire body of work. The Faded Sun is so rich in plot, location, and prose that those traits alone would make it worth reading. The story is exciting and full of wonder. However, the true beauty of this book is in the development of character. I am sure we have all read works in which we enjoyed the story but could have cared less about the characters. This is not the case with Cherryh. The characters come to life. They become the reader's "friends." I cared about what happened to them. Truly an amazing work!</span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_3222668601" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3222668601" />
    <a title="Samantha (AK)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/44733882-samantha-ak"><img alt="Samantha (AK)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1438704616p2/44733882.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3222668601?book_show_action=true">Apr 02, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Samantha (AK)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Samantha (AK)" href="/user/show/44733882-samantha-ak">Samantha (AK)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780613215176" href="/book/show/531121.The_Faded_Sun_Trilogy">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/44733882-samantha-ak?shelf=read-in-2020">read-in-2020</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/44733882-samantha-ak?shelf=setting-sf">setting-sf</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/44733882-samantha-ak?shelf=i-genre-status">i-genre-status</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3222668601" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer132214641273655672">Oh, where do I begin? I suppose first off I should get to the point of things and say "I recommend this."<br/><br/>Yes, you read that right. I'm opening with an endorsement. This is an excellent trilogy, and it fits the omnibus format well.<br/><br/><i>The Faded Sun</i> opens on a desert world, in the eyes of a young alien warrior. His people are the Mri, who have spent their lives in service for the merchant-Regul in a forty-year war against humans, now ended. But with the war over, the Mri are inconvenient, and the Regu</span>
  <span id="freeText132214641273655672" style="display:none">Oh, where do I begin? I suppose first off I should get to the point of things and say "I recommend this."<br /><br />Yes, you read that right. I'm opening with an endorsement. This is an excellent trilogy, and it fits the omnibus format well.<br /><br /><i>The Faded Sun</i> opens on a desert world, in the eyes of a young alien warrior. His people are the Mri, who have spent their lives in service for the merchant-Regul in a forty-year war against humans, now ended. But with the war over, the Mri are inconvenient, and the Regul, fearing what the Mri might do in this new peace, are plotting destruction.<br /><br />Humans, like Regul (or any outsiders), know little of the Mri, having faced only the uncompromising warriors of the Kel caste. Now human envoys are making their way to Kesrith, to cement the new alliance with the Regul and--unknowingly--to shatter an agreement that has stood for two thousand years.<br /><br />I'll admit, the first couple chapters of <i>The Faded Sun</i> gave me strong <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/44767458.Dune__Dune___1_" title="Dune (Dune, #1) by Frank Herbert" rel="nofollow noopener">Dune</a> vibes. The desert setting, the ascestic warrior-race, the intrigue... but it didn't last long. The Mri are not the Fremen, and the remainder of the alien politicking is decidedly not Frank Herbert's inspiration. Perhaps most unique is Cherryh's facility with the construction of her alien races, who are compared to humans not in "worth," but in "kind."<br /><br />The <b>Regul</b> are a Hutt-like, corpulent merchant-race. They have high intellect, long lifespans, and perfect recall, but no imagination. They rely on automated machinery for daily living, and sleds for transportation. Being of limited mobility, they are not a warlike race by nature, but they are fiercely protective of their interests, and willing to use other races to see them through.<br /><br />The <b>Mri</b> are difficult. Closed. Anachronistic. Uncompromising. They do not negotiate. They take no prisoners. They have four words for peace, and not one of them is peace-by-treaty. All who are not Mri are Tsi-mri: "not people." Those outside deal only with Kel-caste--The Face Turned Outward--warriors kept deliberately ignorant of the history and knowledge of The People, so that outsiders may not know The People though them.<br /><br />At the end of the war against humans, there were few Mri left. But the remainder were yet inconvenient. And so the Regul,fearing revenge, saw to have them eliminated entirely... and missed two: A Kel warrior and the last She'pan of the Mri. Together with a single human, these three are set to trace the Mri back to their homeworld, for the sake of survival and knowledge both.<br /><br />I don't know that it's possible to have 'warm and fuzzy' feelings about the Mri, nor do I consider it wise to try. They are a species fully themselves, and violently resistant to change from outside. And yet... through the journey of the character Sten Duncan, we learn admiration. There are the Kath: the childbearing women and their children; and the Sen: the scholars and keepers of history. Each caste of the Mri serves their function, and the overall impression <i>feels</i> like a real people. Subverted is the one-dimensional noble-savage warrior-race! The Mri are hard, but complex.<br /><br />As for Duncan himself, this was a point on which I was pleasantly surprised. It's a poor trope, that a colonial human--often European--joins in with the native race and insodoing becomes their salvior, straddling two worlds and explaining them in a way that outsiders can make palatable. That's not what Cherryh does here. Duncan's path to the Mri is a fascinating journey, and while his presence opens opportunities, the Mri face the crucible on their own terms.<br /><br />This is one trilogy that really <i>should</i> be read in omnibus. Each 'book' feels more a natural part in the narrative, and though some 'recap information' exists, it's minimal, with deft shifts of PoV such that the redundancies feel natural.<br /><br />Some have called the narrative of these books slow-going, or overly introspective. As someone who's read a lot of Cherryh's work in the last year, this is breakneck-speed. Introspective, yes, but not so much it wallows. And the stage is diplomacy, but without endless dialogue and mental explanation of motives. This, fellow readers, is what I call "Accessible C.J. Cherryh." I like her later work well enough, but <i>Wayii</i> the psychological-navel-gazing can be claustrophobic. This was written before she fixated on her 'pale, sweaty man' archetype, and I'm glad for it.<br /><br />Altogether, this is a good read, and one that raises all manner of questions about alien minds and the permissibility of genocide. <br /><br />5 stars, because I'm basking in Happy Book Glow™ and that deserves recognition.</span>
  <a data-text-id="132214641273655672" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_3344682474" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3344682474" />
    <a title="Suz" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2281137-suz"><img alt="Suz" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1311972490p2/2281137.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3344682474?book_show_action=true">Jun 24, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Suz" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Suz" href="/user/show/2281137-suz">Suz</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Audible Audio " href="/book/show/49626580-the-faded-sun-trilogy">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2281137-suz?shelf=scifi">scifi</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2281137-suz?shelf=audio">audio</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3344682474" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6778549936524095182">3+<br/><br/>Cherryh goes above and beyond when it comes to creating alien cultures and sociology, and The Faded Sun Trilogy is no exception to that tendency. The problem was that most of the aliens were pretty unlikable and so it was difficult for me to connect with them more than superficially. Even the Mri, who Cherryh obviously wants us to like, are stubborn and unyielding even to their own detriment. <br/><br/>I listened to this audiobook and the narration was quite good, but I came away from it wondering if I </span>
  <span id="freeText6778549936524095182" style="display:none">3+<br /><br />Cherryh goes above and beyond when it comes to creating alien cultures and sociology, and The Faded Sun Trilogy is no exception to that tendency. The problem was that most of the aliens were pretty unlikable and so it was difficult for me to connect with them more than superficially. Even the Mri, who Cherryh obviously wants us to like, are stubborn and unyielding even to their own detriment. <br /><br />I listened to this audiobook and the narration was quite good, but I came away from it wondering if I would have enjoyed it more if I'd put more focused attention on the story, the way reading the written word demands. I have no doubt that there were subtle layers to relationships in which I missed things, things that make me wonder if a second reading might glean more for me.<br /><br />But the final analysis is that I found the pace slower than I enjoy. So, the bones were there but the sociology alone wasn't enough to make this an overall winner for me. Just ok.</span>
  <a data-text-id="6778549936524095182" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>


      <div class="reviewFooter uitext buttons">

              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9529742303197661318">I find over the years that Cherryh is an author that I continue to enjoy, read and reread. Still I found this series strangely unsettling. Cherryh's characters have a habit of living in your mind well past the "I read it and now I am moving on date", but this time around I find that I am haunted by what I did not know or understand about the main characters. Only Cherryh can write characters of whom I seem to know so little and yet am so greatly haunted and obsessed by.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1686649588" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1686649588" />
    <a title="Lene" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/44017179-lene"><img alt="Lene" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1461013662p2/44017179.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1686649588?book_show_action=true">Jul 03, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lene" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lene" href="/user/show/44017179-lene">Lene</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/44017179-lene?shelf=sf">sf</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1686649588" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4833673167003749247">Damn, I hate this book. I am only finishing it so I can give it a bad review.<br/><br/>I have seen it compared to Dune in other reviews, which usually conclude that it is nothing like Dune. I posit that it is like Dune in all the bad ways, and none of the good.<br/><br/>Central to the book are the mri, an alien species of noble warriors. No, let me rephrase that: genocidal, pompous, primitive, utterly inflexible and utterly implausible savages. You see, they have this ideology that anyone who is not of their specie</span>
  <span id="freeText4833673167003749247" style="display:none">Damn, I hate this book. I am only finishing it so I can give it a bad review.<br /><br />I have seen it compared to Dune in other reviews, which usually conclude that it is nothing like Dune. I posit that it is like Dune in all the bad ways, and none of the good.<br /><br />Central to the book are the mri, an alien species of noble warriors. No, let me rephrase that: genocidal, pompous, primitive, utterly inflexible and utterly implausible savages. You see, they have this ideology that anyone who is not of their species deserves to be killed. Also anyone of their own species who is in any way perceived as weak. They stick with this ideology come hell or high water, unless it suits their interests to sell their services as mercenaries to other species. In this fidelity to their principles they quite vividly remind me of human politicians. <br /><br />It is also against their code of honor to fight in any but the traditional way. This makes them terrible opponents in a sword fight. How their sword fighting abilities help them in a space battle is never touched upon, though. Neither is explored how they can keep a civilization working if everybody is honor-bound to never do any work except fighting. This species, as it is described, is not fit to survive a hundred years. Yet we are supposed to believe it survived a hundred thousand.<br /><br />Granted, in those hundred thousand years it apparently only narrowly escaped self-destruction over a hundred times. Granted also, only two members of the species are left to return to their original, long-forgotten homeworld. Where they encounter the remains of their people who, inexplicably, have kept their old language, laws and rituals to the t. Which is lucky for the protagonists, because it allows them to kill one guy and with that act assume leadership among the locals, in order to restore their people to a supposed, long lost glory.<br /><br />That's about it for the plot. Oh yes, there is also a lot of camping and walking through deserts. But mostly the book is pontificating in pathos-laden language what being a mri is all about (never changing your ways and despising everything foreign). To be honest, as soon as yet another part written from a mri perspective began I tuned out because the language was so self-important and pompous I could not bear it. Also full of made-up words, to add even more fake authenticity.<br /><br />At least The Faded Sun avoided the one thing I hated about Dune the most, the messianic colonialism. The one human among the book's protagonists has not come to lead, but to serve the mri. Which, as you can expect from their attitude, does not go perfectly. He survives by emulating them as closely as possible, finally being accepted as one of them and robbing this book of the last of its protagonists for whom I can feel even the tiniest bit of sympathy. Well, I suppose I am expected to feel sympathy for the mri seeing as they are such noble people. And maybe the humans too, who out of the goodness of their colonialist hearts decide that the mri deserve to survive after all.<br /><br />So, let's see: Boring plot, check. Bad writing, check. Terrible protagonists, check. Extremely dubious ethics, check.<br /><br />There are actually good things about the trilogy, but they don't make up at all for the terribleness. This is the first book I only gave one star on goodreads, and it is thoroughly deserved.</span>
  <a data-text-id="4833673167003749247" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_874340634" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/874340634" />
    <a title="A.B. Gayle" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3050574-a-b-gayle"><img alt="A.B. Gayle" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1277959643p2/3050574.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/874340634?book_show_action=true">Mar 06, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="A.B. Gayle" class="user" itemprop="url" name="A.B. Gayle" href="/user/show/3050574-a-b-gayle">A.B. Gayle</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3050574-a-b-gayle?shelf=science-fiction">science-fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer874340634" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10585122575382703874">Fabulous trilogy. I find it fascinating as a writer the way she starts out deep in the mind of one or two characters, but expands her POV as the series continues.<br/><br/>Most times that would annoy me as I feel I drift away from characters I have come to deeply care about, but the glimpses into minds with totally different attitudes and agendas adds a lot more layers to the story.<br/><br/>Basically this a series about fear. Fear of the unknown, fear of not being true to a way of life (religion?) and fear of that</span>
  <span id="freeText10585122575382703874" style="display:none">Fabulous trilogy. I find it fascinating as a writer the way she starts out deep in the mind of one or two characters, but expands her POV as the series continues.<br /><br />Most times that would annoy me as I feel I drift away from characters I have come to deeply care about, but the glimpses into minds with totally different attitudes and agendas adds a lot more layers to the story.<br /><br />Basically this a series about fear. Fear of the unknown, fear of not being true to a way of life (religion?) and fear of that which can't be controlled.<br /><br />The regul have to be one of the most repugnant races that have ever been written and I must admit Jabba the Hut came to mind when I read that.<br /><br />As for the People? Is there notion of resistance to change and unwillingness to adapt to new ways a good option?<br /><br />I think the final message was that there is no "wrong" or "right" way for a race/species to live, but they have to be true to themselves.<br /><br />It definitely brought into question a lot of aspects pertaining to First Contact and my research of an era when Europeans first came into contact with Maori definitely resonated. The ripples that even the addition of the simple staple, the potato, into their diet caused. Because then they were able to travel a lot further afield, fuelled by a sinpler, stronger source of cabohydrate.<br /><br />In some scholars minds, that had as much bearing on the intertribal wars that followed as the muskets did.<br /><br />In the same way, Duncan's arrival in their midst and his ability to adapt and learn their ways ultimately changed them.<br /><br />My only quibble was the introduction right before the end of the final book of a race that has been around all the time but doesn't get mentioned until they're needed to be. Almost like she was filling a plot hole and needed some means of providing the People with the chance of their HEA. I can see how they fit and their logical, I would have thought that their existence would have been brought in earlier.<br /><br />Also the Dusei that are born to the two that they bring with them seem to grow to adulthood quickly. The passing of time wasn't shown to encompass that. It seemed more like days or at least weeks.</span>
  <a data-text-id="10585122575382703874" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_140143810" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/140143810" />
    <a title="Elizabeth Wallace" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1142024-elizabeth-wallace"><img alt="Elizabeth Wallace" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1536676925p2/1142024.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/140143810?book_show_action=true">Jan 11, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Elizabeth Wallace" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Elizabeth Wallace" href="/user/show/1142024-elizabeth-wallace">Elizabeth Wallace</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1142024-elizabeth-wallace?shelf=sci-fi">sci-fi</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer140143810" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10322560295479386900">In the end I enjoyed it, but my GOODNESS it was a wade. Oddly enough, it was harder to get through than Cherryh's "Foreigner" series, and I don't think it should've been: Foreigner gets WAY deeper into politics and history and plots and such that occasionally go over my head. The Faded Sun Trilogy was very straightforward for the most part but I still found myself checking how much longer until the end of a particular chapter when I got bogged down. Somehow it didn't hold my interest the way the</span>
  <span id="freeText10322560295479386900" style="display:none">In the end I enjoyed it, but my GOODNESS it was a wade. Oddly enough, it was harder to get through than Cherryh's "Foreigner" series, and I don't think it should've been: Foreigner gets WAY deeper into politics and history and plots and such that occasionally go over my head. The Faded Sun Trilogy was very straightforward for the most part but I still found myself checking how much longer until the end of a particular chapter when I got bogged down. Somehow it didn't hold my interest the way the Foreigner cycle does.<br /><br />Once again though, she's created a very interesting race of people, TWO races actually, though of course nobody likes the regul (very sluglike and simpering and unpleasant) and everybody loves the mri (tall, thin, graceful, VERY alien and quiet, with pointed ears...who couldn't like them?) though the mri don't make themselves easy to like, which saves them from being a race of Mary Sue's. They're stubborn, stuck-up (in that honorable "you are beneath my notice" kinda way) and they dislike anybody who isn't a mri...with very certain exceptions. But they're beautiful though, even if they're covered head to foot in black robes and veils. And excellent, dangerous fighters, and they've got that same quiet, rarely-seen sense of humor that the Foreigner atevi have, and when you see it, THAT'S what makes you love them. I guess because you imagine how cool it would be if, for all they dislike humans, they actually liked YOU. I really think that's half of what draws me to both Faded Sun and Foreigner. The other half is Cherryh's amazing attention to detail, and her ability to create these fascinatingly complex aliens (even the regul, as gross as they are, are incredibly interesting.)<br /><br />All in all I'm very glad I read it, but I'm also glad I finished it, finally, and I'll wait for the next Foreigner book very happily.</span>
  <a data-text-id="10322560295479386900" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_131954884" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/131954884" />
    <a title="Dani" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2856252-dani"><img alt="Dani" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1291705519p2/2856252.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/131954884?book_show_action=true">Nov 22, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Dani" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Dani" href="/user/show/2856252-dani">Dani</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2856252-dani?shelf=read-in-2010">read-in-2010</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer131954884" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15046014256938078347">I want to give this book a good review but I just can't seem to do it. I was so torn while reading this book and never once did I care about what would happen. The climax seemed flat to me, without urgency or excitement. Everything took so long to get to that I found myself bored with it. <br/><br/>Also if there is one book that needed a glossary it's this one. It was probably the most confusing first chapter I've ever read in a book. And not confusing plot wise or what the hell is going on wise but the s</span>
  <span id="freeText15046014256938078347" style="display:none">I want to give this book a good review but I just can't seem to do it. I was so torn while reading this book and never once did I care about what would happen. The climax seemed flat to me, without urgency or excitement. Everything took so long to get to that I found myself bored with it. <br /><br />Also if there is one book that needed a glossary it's this one. It was probably the most confusing first chapter I've ever read in a book. And not confusing plot wise or what the hell is going on wise but the simple fact that words are throw at you and never really explained. And things that are mentioned once turn up again but never reexplained so I'm left flipped to the back of the book to see what that one word means to find there is no glossary. Its a little frustrating.<br /><br />Duncan was probably the only character I liked and I found myself just hating mri. I never really cheered for them or wanted them to survive for the sake of the species surviving. To stick it to the regul yes, but for the mri themselves...no. I found myself wanting them to come up against a race better than them, that would say "Fuck you, you can't push us around," and that would be that and the tsi'mri just kill them all. I'm surprised it hasn't happened yet. <br /><br />Combining the slow plot, annoying race, and bland writing style it was just a book that dragged at the end, and that's what really brought it down for me. Sometimes you find yourself up until 2am reading a book because you just can't put it down and you <i>must</i> know how it ends. And something your up until 2am reading because you just don't want to spend another day on this book. Sadly The Faded Sun was the latter and I wished for it to be so much more than it was.<br /><br />Sorry fans, I wanted to like it, I tried to like it. But I just couldn't.</span>
  <a data-text-id="15046014256938078347" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

But soon the galactic stargate will close, isolating Tiamat, and the 150-year reign of the Summer primitives will begin. Their only chance at surviving the change is if Arienrhod, the ageless, corrupt Snow Queen, can destroy destiny with an act of genocide. <div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer17977146287427730593">Currently resident in Spokane, Washington, C.J. Cherryh has won four Hugos and is one of the best-selling and most critically acclaimed authors in the science fiction and fantasy field. She is the author of more than forty novels. Her hobbies include travel, photography, reef culture, Mariners baseball, and, a late passion, figure skating: she intends to compete in the adult USFSA track. She began</span>
  <span id="freeText17977146287427730593" style="display:none">Currently resident in Spokane, Washington, C.J. Cherryh has won four Hugos and is one of the best-selling and most critically acclaimed authors in the science fiction and fantasy field. She is the author of more than forty novels. Her hobbies include travel, photography, reef culture, Mariners baseball, and, a late passion, figure skating: she intends to compete in the adult USFSA track. She began with the modest ambition to learn to skate backwards and now is working on jumps. She sketches, occasionally, cooks fairly well, and hates house work; she loves the outdoors, animals wild and tame, is a hobbyist geologist, adores dinosaurs, and has academic specialties in Roman constitutional law and bronze age Greek ethnography. She has written science fiction since she was ten, spent ten years of her life teaching Latin and Ancient History on the high school level, before retiring to full time writing, and now does not have enough hours in the day to pursue all her interests. Her studies include planetary geology, weather systems, and natural and man-made catastrophes, civilizations, and cosmology…in fact, there's very little that doesn't interest her. A loom is gathering dust and needs rethreading, a wooden ship model awaits construction, and the cats demand their own time much more urgently. She works constantly, researches mostly on the internet, and has books stacked up and waiting to be written. </span>
  <a data-text-id="17977146287427730593" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>
